Commun.</a></span>, 2024, <strong>60</strong>, 5010-5013</div><h1 id="sect188"><span class="title_heading">A porous organic polymer for symmetric sodium dual-ion batteries through an adsorption-intercalation-insertion mechanism<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a></span></h1><p class="header_text">
      <span class="bold">

            Abhijit 
            Patra
          
        
      </span><span class="orcid"><a target="_blank" title="Select to open ORCID record for Abhijit&nbsp;Patra (orcid.org/0000-0003-3144-1813) in a new window" id="connect-orcid-link" href="http://orcid.org/0000-0003-3144-1813"><img id="orcid-id-logo" src="/content/NewImages/orcid_16x16.png" alt="ORCID logo"></a></span>*<sup><span class="sup_ref italic">a</span></sup>
      <br><a id="affa"><sup><span class="sup_ref italic">a</span></sup></a><span class="italic">Department of Chemistry, Indian Institute of Science Education and Research Bhopal, Bhauri, Bhopal, Madhya Pradesh 462066, India. E-mail: <a href="mailto:abhijit@iiserb.ac.in">abhijit@iiserb.ac.in</a></span>
      <br><a id="affb"><sup><span class="sup_ref italic">b</span></sup></a><span class="italic">Chemistry Division, Bhabha Atomic Research Centre, Mumbai-400 085, India</span>
    </p><div id="art-admin"><span class="italic bold">Received 
      7th February 2024
    </span><span class="bold italic">, Accepted 21st March 2024</span></div><p class="bold italic">First published on 21st March 2024</p><hr><div class="abstract"><h2>Abstract</h2><p>A porous organic polymer (POP) has been developed for dual-ion storage in all organic symmetric rechargeable batteries. The triphenylamine-pyrene-based POP could host sodium and hexafluorophosphate ions acting as the anode and the cathode, respectively, through the adsorption-intercalation and insertion mechanism. The current study highlights the concept of widening the potential window of a dual ion battery by judicious selection of the constituent moieties.</p></div><hr>
    
      <span>Harvesting renewable energies is the need of the hour to mitigate the increasing energy demand. Developing off-grid portable clean energy storage devices, such as rechargeable metal-ion batteries, is one of the promising solutions.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit1"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1</span></sup></a> In general, rechargeable metal-ion batteries involve the shuttling of metal ions between the cathode (metal-ion source) and the anode (metal-ion host), thus requiring separate fabrication of each electrode.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit2"><sup><span class="sup_ref">2</span></sup></a> Recently, the concept of dual-ion batteries, avoiding the use of an alkali-metal-rich cathode, has been introduced.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit3"><sup><span class="sup_ref">3</span></sup></a> The electrolyte used in dual-ion batteries solely supplies the required cations and anions.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit4"><sup><span class="sup_ref">4</span></sup></a> In this case, simultaneous hosting of the cations and anions in the anode and cathode reduces the overall inactive mass of the electrode in the cell compared to the regular metal-ion batteries.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit5"><sup><span class="sup_ref">5</span></sup></a> This improves the energy density of the cell. The use of the same electrode material in both the cathode and anode leads to symmetric dual-ion batteries (SDIBs, <a title="Select to navigate to scheme" href="#imgsch1">Scheme 1</a>), further simplifying the battery fabrication and operational cost, leading to a high commercial value.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit4"><sup><span class="sup_ref">4</span></sup></a></span>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgsch1"><a href="/image/article/2024/CC/d4cc00642a/d4cc00642a-s1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4cc00642a-s1.tif" src="/image/article/2024/CC/d4cc00642a/d4cc00642a-s1.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Scheme 1 </b> <span id="sch1"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Schematic illustration of previously explored symmetric dual-ion batteries (SDIBs) using intercalation-type π-conjugated carbon materials or insertion-type small organic molecules as electrode materials. (b) The present work depicting porous organic polymers by linking pyrene for Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ion storage through adsorption-intercalation and triphenylamine for PF<small><sub>6</sub></small><small><sup>−</sup></small> ion storage through insertion for all organic SDIBs.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The previous strategies for the fabrication of all organic SDIBs involve the development of symmetric organic molecules having p-type and n-type moieties either linked or fused together.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit6"><sup><span class="sup_ref">6</span></sup></a> Furthermore, a wide working electrochemical window is desirable to improve the energy density of the cell.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit7"><sup><span class="sup_ref">7</span></sup></a> This can be achieved by increasing the cathode potential or, decreasing the anode potential or both simultaneously.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit8"><sup><span class="sup_ref">8</span></sup></a> The sodiation/lithiation potentials for the intercalation-type anodes (graphite, hard carbons, polyaromatic hydrocarbons) are found to be lower than those of the insertion-type organic anodes (<span class="italic">i.e.</span>, having redox-active moieties).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit9"><sup><span class="sup_ref">9</span></sup></a> On the other hand, in the quest for efficient electrode materials, redox-active POPs have been found to satisfy some of the key energy storage performance metrics.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit10"><sup><span class="sup_ref">10</span></sup></a> POPs have been used in a wide range of applications ranging from water purification, catalysis and light harvesting, to energy storage, including batteries and supercapacitors.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit11"><sup><span class="sup_ref">11</span></sup></a> The flexibility in design and fabrication, tunable porosity, and well-defined redox properties of POPs are promising for their use as both cathode and anode materials.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit12"><sup><span class="sup_ref">12</span></sup></a> Thus, incorporating polyaromatic hydrocarbons and insertion-type cathode-active components into a porous network could be a worthwhile strategy in developing organic electrodes for SDIBs.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">Herein, we have developed a triphenylamine-pyrene-based nitrogen-rich redox-active porous organic polymer (TPA-Py, <a title="Select to navigate to scheme" href="#imgsch1">Scheme 1</a>) for sodium-based organic SDIBs. The TPA-Py polymer possesses pyrene units for Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> adsorption and triphenylamine moieties for hexafluorophosphate ion (PF<small><sub>6</sub></small><small><sup>−</sup></small>) insertion.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit13"><sup><span class="sup_ref">13</span></sup></a> The TPA-Py POP was employed for both the anode and cathode using half-cells, and finally, a symmetric all-organic full-cell battery was fabricated. The current study, to the best of our knowledge, is the first report on a sodium-based SDIB with POP having adsorption-intercalation-type anode and insertion-type cathode components, resulting in a wide working potential window.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">The POP was synthesized by the cross-coupling reaction between 4,4′,4′′-triaminotriphenylamine (TPA) and 1,3,6,8-tetrabromopyrene (Py) using palladium-catalysed Buchwald–Hartwig coupling (Scheme S1, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit14"><sup><span class="sup_ref">14</span></sup></a> The Fourier transform infrared (FTIR) spectroscopic analysis of the resulting TPA-Py POP showed a noticeable shift of the C–N bending vibrational band from 1612 cm<small><sup>−1</sup></small> of TPA to 1592 cm<small><sup>−1</sup></small> and the disappearance of the characteristic band at 3240–3460 cm<small><sup>−1</sup></small> for N–H stretching of primary amines, suggesting C–N linkage formation (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1a</a>). Furthermore, the disappearance of the band at 1056 cm<small><sup>−1</sup></small> of C–Br stretching in TPA-Py ascertained the successful polymer formation (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1a</a>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit14b"><sup><span class="sup_ref">14b</span></sup></a> The solid-state <small><sup>13</sup></small>C-cross-polarization magic angle spinning (CP-MAS) nuclear magnetic resonance (NMR) spectrum of TPA-Py revealed the closely-spaced characteristic peaks at ∼145 and 139 ppm from the carbons connected to the nitrogen atoms (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1b</a>). In contrast, the closely-spaced intense peaks around 128 and 125 ppm could be attributed to the aromatic carbons (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1b</a>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit14a"><sup><span class="sup_ref">14a</span></sup></a></p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig1"><a href="/image/article/2024/CC/d4cc00642a/d4cc00642a-f1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4cc00642a-f1.tif" src="/image/article/2024/CC/d4cc00642a/d4cc00642a-f1.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 1 </b> <span id="fig1"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Comparative FTIR spectra of TPA-Py porous polymers with constituent monomers, tris(4-aminophenyl)amine (TPA-3NH<small><sub>2</sub></small>), and 1,3,6,8-tetrabromopyrene (Py-4Br). (b) Solid-state <small><sup>13</sup></small>C NMR spectrum (CP-MAS) of TPA-Py POP. (c) Nitrogen adsorption–desorption isotherms of TPA-Py POP at 77 K. (d) Thermogravimetric analysis profile of TPA-Py POP indicating a high thermal stability. (e) Field emission scanning electron microscopy image and high-resolution transmission electron microscopy image of TPA-Py POP (inset).</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) surface area of TPA-Py was found to be 70 m<small><sup>2</sup></small> g<small><sup>−1</sup></small> from the N<small><sub>2</sub></small> adsorption isotherm (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1c</a> and Fig. S1, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>). The pore size distribution analysis revealed hierarchical porosity with both micropores and a wide range of mesopores (Fig. S2, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>). The high thermal stability up to 320 °C, as evidenced by the thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) profile, suggests a promising scope of TPA-Py POP as an electrode material in high-temperature energy storage devices (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1d</a>). It also provides a higher safety margin against accidental temperature rise.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit15"><sup><span class="sup_ref">15</span></sup></a> The TPA-Py POP appeared as irregular fused globular particles under field emission scanning electron microscopy (FESEM, <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1e</a>). The high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) images also show a connected network architecture, typical for amorphous porous organic polymers (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1e</a>, inset). The broad powder X-ray diffraction profile further substantiated the amorphous nature of the TPA-Py polymer (Fig. S3, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>).</p>
      <p class="otherpara">The electrochemical performances of the TPA-Py polymer for dual-ion battery applications were investigated by fabricating half-cells (using Na-metal as a reference as well as a counter electrode and 1 M NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small> in diglyme as an electrolyte). The cyclic voltammogram (CV) of the TPA-Py polymer was analysed in the potential window of 0.01 to 4.2 V (Fig. S7, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>). The CV profile of the TPA-Py polymer shows redox-active regions at two extreme potentials, suggesting its intrinsic nature for dual-ion storage.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit6"><sup><span class="sup_ref">6</span></sup></a> The potential range 0.01–2.5 V was chosen as anodic, whereas 2.5–4.2 V was chosen for the cathodic regions of the POP-based cell. The CV of the cell during the anodic scan revealed a strong and broad irreversible reduction peak between ∼0.3 and 0.9 V in the first CV cycle, representing the electrolyte decomposition and the solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) formation (Fig. S8, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit13a"><sup><span class="sup_ref">13a</span></sup></a> A prominent reversible redox peak at the lower potential of the CV of the anodic scan below 0.2 V, as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2a</a>, suggests the adsorption-intercalation of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions at the pyrene moieties and pore filling of TPA-Py POP (Fig. S14, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit16"><sup><span class="sup_ref">16</span></sup></a> The current responses increased with higher scan rates suggesting faster sodiation/desodiation processes.</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig2"><a href="/image/article/2024/CC/d4cc00642a/d4cc00642a-f2_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4cc00642a-f2.tif" src="/image/article/2024/CC/d4cc00642a/d4cc00642a-f2.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 2 </b> <span id="fig2"><span class="graphic_title">Scan rate-dependent cyclic voltammograms of TPA-Py POP for Na-ion batteries as the (a) anode (potential window: 0.01–2.5 V) and (b) cathode (potential window: 2.5–4.2 V). Galvanostatic charge–discharge profiles of TPA-Py POP at different current densities as the (c) anode and (d) cathode. Galvanostatic rate capability profiles of TPA-Py POP as the (e) anode and (f) cathode at different current densities from 20 to 2000 mA g<small><sup>−1</sup></small> (20, 50, 100, 200, 500, 1000 and 2000 mA g<small><sup>−1</sup></small>) and back to 20 mA g<small><sup>−1</sup></small>.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The capacitive contribution of TPA-Py POP for Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ion storage estimated using Dunn's method varies from ∼46% to 73%, as shown in Fig. S9 (ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>). The major diffusion contribution (intercalation process) appears at significantly lower potential (&lt;0.25 V). In contrast, the capacitive contribution comes majorly in the potential range ∼0.25 to 2.0 V. Thus, the simultaneous contribution from adsorption and intercalation facilitates Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ion storage by TPA-Py POP for a wider potential window. On the other hand, the two distinct redox peaks having <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>1/2</sub></small> values of 3.1 V and 3.9 V in the CV of the cathodic scan signify the two-stage anion storage of the polymer. The peaks at ∼3.2 V and ∼4.0 V indicate the oxidation of tertiary nitrogen of triphenylamine moieties and secondary nitrogen of the bridging –NH-groups in the polymer,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit17"><sup><span class="sup_ref">17</span></sup></a> respectively (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2b</a>). Upon oxidation, the triphenylamine moieties reversibly store two PF<small><sub>6</sub></small><small><sup>−</sup></small> ions of the electrolyte through an anion-insertion mechanism, resulting in a quinoidal structure (Fig. S15, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit13b"><sup><span class="sup_ref">13b</span></sup></a> Thus, the polymer could store dual-ions, <span class="italic">i.e.</span>, Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> and PF<small><sub>6</sub></small><small><sup>−</sup></small>, through the adsorption-intercalation and insertion mechanism, respectively, during charging.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">The specific capacity of the POP was similarly measured by making a half-cell for the anode and cathode by galvanostatic charge–discharge (GCD) experiments at different scan rates ranging from 20 to 2000 mA g<small><sup>−1</sup></small>. The first discharge cycle of the polymer as the anode exhibits a plateau near ∼0.9 V, corresponding to the SEI formation (Fig. S10, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>), which corroborates well with the CV data (Fig. S8, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>). The GCD profiles of the polymer in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2c and d</a> show a decrease in specific capacity for both the anode and cathode, respectively, with increasing current density. The highest reversible capacities of the TPA-Py polymer as the anode and cathode at 20 mA g<small><sup>−1</sup></small> are 109 and 65 mA h g<small><sup>−1</sup></small>, respectively (Table S2, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>). Furthermore, an appreciable rate capability was observed using TPA-Py POP in the case of anodic reaction (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2e</a>). However, the rate capability has been impacted slightly during the cathodic reactions (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2f</a>). The insertion of bulky PF<small><sub>6</sub></small><small><sup>−</sup></small> ions in TPA-Py POP not only imparts a large volume change of the electrode but can get blocked in the narrow pores of the polymer resulting in sluggish electrode kinetics.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit18"><sup><span class="sup_ref">18</span></sup></a></p>
      <p class="otherpara">The galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was employed at different potentials to elucidate further the diffusion of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> and PF<small><sub>6</sub></small><small><sup>−</sup></small> ions in the polymer matrix (Fig. S12, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit19"><sup><span class="sup_ref">19</span></sup></a> The calculated diffusion coefficients of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (<span class="italic">D</span><small><sub>Na+</sub></small>) and PF<small><sub>6</sub></small><small><sup>−</sup></small> (<span class="italic">D</span><small><sub>PF6</sub></small>−) are ∼10<small><sup>−12</sup></small> to 10<small><sup>−14</sup></small> cm<small><sup>2</sup></small> s<small><sup>−1</sup></small> and ∼10<small><sup>−12</sup></small> to 10<small><sup>−15</sup></small> cm<small><sup>2</sup></small> s<small><sup>−1</sup></small>, respectively. To evaluate the charge-transfer resistance of the polymer during charging, potentiostatic electrochemical impedance spectroscopic (EIS) measurement was carried out at different potentials. In the Nyquist plots of TPA-Py POP (Fig. S13, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>), the small semi-circle represents the charge transfer resistance (<span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>CT</sub></small>), whereas the inclined straight line refers to the Warburg impedance (<span class="italic">Z</span><small><sub>W</sub></small>). With increasing the DC bias, the <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>CT</sub></small> decreases, indicating faster charge transfer in the polymer matrix using it both as an anode and cathode.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit20"><sup><span class="sup_ref">20</span></sup></a></p>
      <p class="otherpara">The TPA-Py POP showed ∼85% and ∼80% capacity retention after 1000 GCD cycles with respect to the initial capacities for the anodic and cathodic reactions, respectively (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3a</a>). This slight capacity loss might be due to the ohmic resistance increase (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3b</a> and Fig. S11a, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>), electrode pulverization, and some extent of pore-clogging during the charge–discharge process by Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> and PF<small><sub>6</sub></small><small><sup>−</sup></small> ions.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit21"><sup><span class="sup_ref">21</span></sup></a> The coulombic efficiency for both the cathodic and anodic reactions remained stable in the range of 96–100% after the initial few cycles (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3a</a>). Based on the cation and anion storage ability of TPA-Py POP, a sodium-based symmetric dual-ion battery was fabricated, where TPA-Py POP was used as both the cathode and anode (Fig. S14 and S15, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>). The electrochemical performance of a symmetric dual-ion battery is shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3c</a> (Fig. S11b, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>).</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig3"><a href="/image/article/2024/CC/d4cc00642a/d4cc00642a-f3_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4cc00642a-f3.tif" src="/image/article/2024/CC/d4cc00642a/d4cc00642a-f3.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 3 </b> <span id="fig3"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Cycling stability of TPA-Py POP as the anode and cathode at a current density of 200 mA g<small><sup>−1</sup></small> and the corresponding coulombic efficiencies for 1000 cycles. (b) Nyquist plots of TPA-Py POP as the anode (green) and cathode (blue) before and after 1000 galvanostatic charge–discharge (GCD) cycles. (c) GCD profiles of a symmetric dual-ion battery employing TPA-Py polymer as the cathode and anode with 1 M NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small> in diglyme at 20 mA g<small><sup>−1</sup></small>.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The electronic structure of the building units and repeating unit of the polymer were computed using density functional theory calculation [B3LYP, 6-31G(d,p)] to get more insights into the electronic distributions. The smaller HOMO–LUMO energy gap of TPA-Py indicates higher electronic conduction compared to its monomers, resulting in enhanced electronic conductivity and faster redox kinetics in the porous polymer (Fig. S17, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit13a"><sup><span class="sup_ref">13a</span></sup></a> The molecular electrostatic potential (MESP)-mapped electron density calculation of the repeating unit revealed the preferred localization of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions near the pyrene units and PF<small><sub>6</sub></small><small><sup>−</sup></small> closer to triphenylamine units (Fig. S18, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>).</p>
      <p class="otherpara">The mechanistic investigation of dual-ion storage by the TPA-Py polymer was carried out using <span class="italic">ex situ</span> FTIR analysis of the battery electrodes. The strong absorption peaks at 1495 cm<small><sup>−1</sup></small> (C<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_e001.gif" alt="[double bond, length as m-dash]">C) decreased substantially after discharging to 0.01 V, and two new peaks appeared at 1427 and 879 cm<small><sup>−1</sup></small>, suggesting the n-doping of the pyrene moieties during Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ion storage.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit13a"><sup><span class="sup_ref">13a</span></sup></a> On the other hand, when the TPA-Py POP containing half-cell was charged to 4.2 V, two new characteristic peaks appeared. The peaks at 1660 and 840 cm<small><sup>−1</sup></small> could be attributed to the stretching vibration of C<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_e001.gif" alt="[double bond, length as m-dash]">N from one of the possible quinoid-like structures of triphenylamine moieties,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit17"><sup><span class="sup_ref">17</span></sup></a> and P–F stretching vibration, respectively (Fig. S16, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit22"><sup><span class="sup_ref">22</span></sup></a> Thus, the dual-ion charge storage process by TPA-Py POP has been ascertained through the adsorption-intercalation-insertion mechanism (Fig. S16, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1">†</a>).</p>
      <p class="otherpara">In summary, we have designed a novel porous organic polymer (TPA-Py) containing both anode and cathode active units for dual-ion batteries. The pyrene units in the polymer facilitate reversible Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ion adsorption-intercalation, and the redox-active triphenylamine units in the network assist in the reversible storage of PF<small><sub>6</sub></small><small><sup>−</sup></small> ions. As a proof of concept, we have fabricated a symmetrical dual ion battery using TPA-Py polymer in both the cathode and anode. The present study employing a porous organic polymer as an adsorption-intercalation-type anode and the insertion-type cathode lights the way for further exploration of symmetric dual-ion batteries with a wide potential window leading to high energy density.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">We thank SERB (project no. CRG/2021/008526) for the financial support and IISERB for the infrastructural support. SS thanks IISERB for the Institute Post-doctoral Fellowship (IPDF) and other group members for valuable suggestions.</p>

            <br><a href="https://cookiepedia.co.uk/giving-consent-to-cookies" class="privacy-notice-link" rel="noopener" target="_blank" aria-label="More information about your privacy, opens in a new tab">More information</a></div><button id="accept-recommended-btn-handler">Allow all</button><section class="ot-sdk-row ot-cat-grp"><h3 id="ot-category-title"> Manage consent preferences</h3><div class="ot-pli-hdr ot-leg-border-color"><span class="ot-li-title">Consent</span> <span class="ot-li-title">Legitimate interest</span></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0001"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0001" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0001 ot-status-id-C0001"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0001">Strictly necessary cookies</h4></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0001">These cookies are necessary for the website to function and cannot be switched off in our systems. They are usually only set in response to actions made by you which amount to a request for services, such as setting your privacy preferences, logging in or filling in forms. You can set your browser to block or alert you about these cookies, but some parts of the site will not then work. These cookies do not store any personally identifiable information.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0002"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0002" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0002"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0002">Analytical cookies</h4><div class="ot-tgl"><input type="checkbox" name="ot-group-id-C0002" id="ot-group-id-C0002" role="switch" class="category-switch-handler" data-optanongroupid="C0002" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0002"> <label class="ot-switch" for="ot-group-id-C0002"><span class="ot-switch-nob"></span> <span class="ot-label-txt">Analytical cookies</span></label> </div></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0002">These cookies allow us to count visits and traffic sources so we can measure and improve the performance of our site. They help us to know which pages are the most and least popular and see how visitors move around the site. All information these cookies collect is aggregated and therefore anonymous. If you do not allow these cookies we will not know when you have visited our site, and will not be able to monitor its performance.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0003"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0003" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0003"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0003">Functional cookies</h4><div class="ot-tgl"><input type="checkbox" name="ot-group-id-C0003" id="ot-group-id-C0003" role="switch" class="category-switch-handler" data-optanongroupid="C0003" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0003"> <label class="ot-switch" for="ot-group-id-C0003"><span class="ot-switch-nob"></span> <span class="ot-label-txt">Functional cookies</span></label> </div></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0003">These cookies enable the website to provide enhanced functionality and personalisation.
